  27. Oral-B has a number of brushes available - the Sonic, Vitality, the Professional Care family (which comprises the 1000 and 3000), and the Professional Care SmartSeries (4000 and 5000). The Oral-B 1000 is the entry level of the Professional Care series.<br /><br />In my usage of the Vitality and the Oral-B 1000, the Oral-B 1000 stands at the minimum level of functionality to make an electric toothbrush viable.<br /><br />In particular, note that the Vitality does not have a quadrant timer (it beeps only at the end of the 2-minute cycle), is rated at only 7600 oscillations per minute, and does not have a battery charging indicator. All of which are present just one level up in the Professional Care 1000.<br /><br />To me the lack of a quadrant timer is a big disappointment - I don't want to be watching a clock while brushing if I don't have to. The gentle thrumming of the Professional Care 1000 every 30 seconds is a very nice pacer.<br /><br />The brushes in the Professional Care series not only add quadrant timers, but also are rated both at 8800 oscillations per minute and at 40,000 pulsations per minute, and have battery charge indicators.<br /><br />As you go higher in the Professional Care family you get multiple brush modes (daily clean, sensitive, polish, deep clean), pressure sensors, and even wireless displays.<br /><br />Overall, I found the Vitality to be lacking features that I rely on. Hence my rating. I'd strongly recommend that you consider the Professional Care 1000 as the minimum entry level functionality for a brush. You'll probably find (like I did) that you don't need much more than what the Professional Care 1000 has to offer.<br /><br />Happy Brushing!

  33. Overall, the Vitality is a nice toothbrush. If one trusts the packaging, it out performs a manual toothbrush. If price is your main concern, the Vitality is a good choice. The included brush heads (the ones with the polishing cup) are unsatisfactory, however. The brush has too strong a vibration inside the mouth; almost as if it bouncing of teeth instead of polishing them. It's a noisy head, to boot. When I switched to a regular brush head, the vibrations and bounce significantly declined. The Vitality does have its faults; especially when compared to the higher end Braun/Oral Bs. First, the motor is not as smooth as the other brushes. It does not seem to vibrate at as fast a rate as my other more expensive Braun. When I compared Vitality with my other Braun (without brush heads) it was easy to see the Vitality simply vibrates more slowly and without as much power. My other Braun is much smoother during brushing. This smoothness means the brush bristles maintain more contact with one's teeth during brushing. I am not happy with the timer. It does not have the 30 second notifiers like my other Braun. I have to keep track of time in my head. The 30 second timers ensure one is able to brush all one's teeth within the two minute span. I am sure cost kept this feature from the Vitality. The NiCd battery within the vitality is also a weak point. Unlike the nickle metal hydride battery in the up-level Braun/Oral B units, the NiCd takes longer to charge, suffers from battery memory, should be fully discharged before recharging, and cannot store as much power as an NiMH. There is no included charge indicator light, as well. So, it's a decent brush for the budget conscious. However, for a much better experience, look at the higher end Braun/Oral Bs.

  75. Powered brushes are shockingly expensive and this is the cheapest Oral-B model. The brush and plug-in charger are two separate units. The charger has a small footprint and low profile, with a sealed chassis and contact point, keeping water out. The brush handle is about the diameter of a broom handle, with a lot of rubber to protect it from water and to keep it from slipping out of your wet hand. The clicking on-off button is sealed in rubber and the contact point in the handle is also completely sealed. The only point where water might get in is where the brush meets the handle. Charging is idiot-proof: mount the brush (no skill involved) and you're ready for next time. Sealed contacts allow you to rinse or wipe off the handle or charger. The brush cycle pauses quickly when two minutes have passed and teeth are clean. The Vitality is durable - it still holds a charge and brushes effectively after over a year. I replaced the original single brush with [[ASIN:B002BTETG4 Oral-B Dual Clean 6 Replacement Brush Head]] replacements, which are a little larger than original equipment (maybe too large for some?), but a little more effective. Just don't completely immerse either component in water and you'll be good to go. Cheap, simple, unobtrusive, effective - what else could you want?

  98. The Oral-B's VITALITY offers decent value but it doesn't come close to the 'high end' performance and convenience offered (at a higher price) by rival products such as Sonicare.<br /><br />So, for the GOOD qualities:<br /><br />- Rechargeable - I view this as a 'bottom line' feature when it comes to electric toothbrushes and VITALITY has it.<br />- Water-proof - the body appears to be fully sealed. Like Sonicare, this model is using the 'proximity' charge method where you place the toothbrush's body on the base and charging takes place when the base is plugged into an electric outlet.<br />- Extra brush - this model comes with 2 brushes, one mounted on the body and one extra.<br />- Easy brush replacement - you simply pull the mounted brush to take it out, push the new one in.<br />- $3 coupon to be used when purchasing replacement brush heads.<br /><br />Not so good or annoying:<br /><br />- The packaging is atrocious. It comes in one of those bullet-proof clear plastic enclosures that you must cut with scissors and make sure you don't cut yourself in the sharp edges while at it. It took me several minutes to extract the contents off packaging and I did manage to do it scratch-free.<br />- Vibrations are a little too strong - this MIGHT be my Sonicare bias (which I've been using for longer than I can remember) but I felt that this VITALITY was a little too aggressive. My teeth are a little bit sensitive and they didn't like that.<br />- A little too noisy for what I am used to - of course, an 'ultrasonic' toothbrush noise is harder to detect because... it's ultrasound.<br /><br />When compared to the higher-end products, it may be worth noting that the VITALITY does not come with a 'full' timer. The toothbrush does tell you when the 2 minutes are up (noise similar to revving an engine) but it does not turn itself off and, more importantly, it does not give you 30-second signals so you can switch 'quadrants' as the higher end products do.<br /><br />The VITALITY offers a lot for the price but I am not sure that 'price' is THAT meaningful when the topic is our teeth. It's probably preferable to most manual toothbrushes but, for a few dollars more you can get a lot better. Overall this is a decent product but if I had to replace my higher end toothbrush today, knowing what I know after trying out this product I would NOT go for the VITALITY and sacrifice features and convenience. The few dollars saved would not justify it.<br /><br />Three stars, meaning \\"It's Okay\\" seem to be the fair rating on the Amazon scale.ers a lot for the price but I am not sure that 'price' is THAT meaningful when the topic is our teeth. It's probably preferable to most manual toothbrushes but, for a few dollars more you can get a lot better. It also lacks a lot of the frills of the other toothbrush. No LED light to indicating charging / charge full, and it does not pulse at 30 second intervals when brushing. I'm giving it 4 stars despite the shortcomings because it is significantly cheaper than the other toothbrush. I think they balance each other out (I'd rate my existing toothbrush 4 stars as well).   147. This is my fourth Braun Oral B electric toothbrush.<br /><br />I have had several entry level models over the years, replacing each of them when the internal battery had reached the end of its working life.<br /><br />My dentist recommended that I use an electric toothbrush, and this entry level model has proven to be entirely satisfactory.<br /><br />The principal features are:<br /><br />1. It uses replaceable brush heads. It fits a variety of the brush heads which Oral B offers, but you should ensure that you do not buy one of the heads which don't fit this model! Also, there are several generic substitute brush heads available.<br /><br />2. It is powered by a non-replaceable rechargeable battery, which is sealed inside the handle. You charge the toothbrush by placing the handle on a compact bench top charger. Charging is by induction, do there are no metal contacts to corrode.<br /><br />3. The charger requires a 110V power source for US market models. This does restrict its usage when you are travelling overseas, where the mains power source is 220-240V. If you are a significant traveler, I recommend you consider one of the more expensive models which have dual power source compatibility.<br /><br />4. A charge will last about a week before needing a recharge.<br /><br />5. The handle incorporates a 2 minute timer: this works by vibrating briefly when the toothbrush has been operated for two minutes.<br /><br />6. The brush heads- depending on type, and how you brush- last about 2-3 months. Some Oral B brushes incorporate a wear indicator, to help you to ascertain when replacement is necessary.<br /><br />7. In my experience, these toothbrushes will last about 2-3 years before requiring replacement. The packaging includes information regarding safe disposal and recycling.<br /><br />There are more expensive electric toothbrushes available, which do have additional functional attributes and accessories. For some people, these may be necessary or worthwhile.<br /><br />However, I suspect most people would find this entry level model to suit their requirements./><br />However, I suspect most people would find this entry level model to suit their requirements.

  390. I bought two of these to replace my old Oral Bs whose batteries failed after about 7 years of use. My only reservation with the new ones is that they don't have a charging indicator light, but I'm getting used to that as charging works just fine. You just have to be sure the charger is plugged in to a live outlet. For those who care, the Vitality Pro is made in Mexico, the old brushes were from Germany.<br />I experimented with one of my old chargers and found that it's compatible with this toothbrush and charges at the same rate as the supplied chargers, even though the old one is capable of putting out twice the charge rate*, which the old toothbrush needed, having a higher-capacity NiMH battery.<br />Compatibility note: The chargers have the rounded-corner-trapezoid charging peg. The old chargers are wall-mountable and have the brush-head holder whereas the new ones are smaller and easier to pack for travel but have no wall mount or brush holder.<br />The new brushes provide the same action, feel and (I believe) speed, so they are a good replacement. They are single-speed, but I never used the low speed on my old brushes anyway.<br /><br />* I compared the charge-rate capabilities indirectly by winding a coil to fit over the charging pegs and measuring the induced voltages, which were 2:1 (old:new). The actual charge rates were roughly measured for each charger by running the brush to battery exhaustion (the point at which the brush stops running), charging 1 hour, and measuring the run times until reaching exhaustion again (both were equal). This suggests that the new brush has some sort of charge-rate control to prevent over-fast charging, for the sake of battery life.<br />All in all, a decent brush at a bargain price!
